<p>Despite
Gahan's
increasingly
severe
personal
problems,
Gore
tried
repeatedly
during
1995
and
1996
to
get
the
band
recording
again.
However,
Gahan
would
rarely
turn
up
to
scheduled
sessions,
and
when
he
did,
it
would
take
weeks
to
get
any
vocals
recorded.
One
six-week
session
at
<a
href="/wiki/Electric_Lady_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Electric
Lady
Studios">Electric
Lady</a>
in
New
York
produced
just
one
usable
vocal
(for
&quot;Sister
Of
Night&quot;),
and
even
that
was
pieced
together
from
multiple
takes.<sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup>
Gore
was
forced
to
contemplate
breaking
the
band
up,
and
releasing
the
songs
he
had
written
as
a
solo
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
mid-1996,
Gahan
entered
a
court
ordered
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
rehabilitation">drug
rehabilitation</a>
program
to
battle
his
cocaine-heroin
addiction
after
his
near
fatal
overdose.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
With
Gahan
out
of
rehab
in
1996,
Depeche
Mode
held
recording
sessions
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_Simenon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
Simenon">Tim
Simenon</a>.
The
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Ultra_(Depeche_Mode_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ultra
(Depeche
Mode
album)">Ultra</a></i>
was
released
in
April
1997,
its
release
was
preceded
by
two
singles,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Barrel_of_a_Gun_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barrel
of
a
Gun
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Barrel
of
a
Gun</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It%27s_No_Good?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It's
No
Good">It's
No
Good</a>&quot;.
The
album
debuted
at
No.
1
in
the
UK
(as
well
as
Germany),
and
No.
5
in
the
US.
The
band
did
not
tour
in
support
of
the
album
but
as
part
of
the
promotion
for
its
release
they
did
perform
two
short
concerts
in
London
and
Los
Angeles
called
Ultra
Parties.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Ultra</i>
spawned
two
further
singles,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Home_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Home
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Home</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Useless_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Useless
(song)">Useless</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>A
second
singles
compilation
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Singles_86%E2%80%9398?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Singles
86–98">The
Singles
86–98</a></i>
was
released
in
1998,
preceded
by
the
new
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Only_When_I_Lose_Myself?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Only
When
I
Lose
Myself">Only
When
I
Lose
Myself</a>&quot;,
which
had
been
recorded
during
the
<i>Ultra</i>
sessions.
In
April
1998
Depeche
Mode
held
a
press
conference
at
the
Hyatt
Hotel
in
<a
href="/wiki/Cologne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cologne">Cologne</a>
to
announce
<a
href="/wiki/The_Singles_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Singles
Tour">The
Singles
Tour</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-67"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
tour
was
the
first
one
to
feature
two
backing
musicians
in
place
of
Alan
Wilder
–
Austrian
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Christian_Eigner?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christian
Eigner">Christian
Eigner</a>
and
British
keyboardist
<a
href="/wiki/Peter_Gordeno_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peter
Gordeno
(musician)">Peter
Gordeno</a>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Exciter_.282001.E2.80.932004.29"><i>Exciter</i>
(2001–2004)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11"
title="Edit
section:
Exciter
(2001–2004)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
2001,
Depeche
Mode
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Exciter_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Exciter
(album)">Exciter</a></i>,
which
was
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Bell_(British_musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mark
Bell
(British
musician)">Mark
Bell</a>
(of
the
pioneering
<a
href="/wiki/Techno?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Techno">techno</a>
group
<a
href="/wiki/LFO_(British_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LFO
(British
band)">LFO</a>).
Bell
introduced
a
minimalist,
digital
sound
to
much
of
the
album,
influenced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Intelligent_dance_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Intelligent
dance
music">IDM</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Glitch_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Glitch
(music)">glitch</a>.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dream_On_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dream
On
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Dream
On</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Feel_Loved?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Feel
Loved">I
Feel
Loved</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Freelove?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Freelove">Freelove</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Goodnight_Lovers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Goodnight
Lovers">Goodnight
Lovers</a>&quot;
were
released
as
singles
in
2001
and
2002.
The
critical
response
to
the
album
was
mixed.
Whilst
it
received
reasonably
positive
reviews
from
some
magazines
(<i><a
href="/wiki/NME?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NME">NME</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/LA_Weekly?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LA
Weekly">LA
Weekly</a></i>),
others
(including
<i>Q</i>
magazine,
<a
href="/wiki/PopMatters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pitchfork
Media">Pitchfork
Media</a>)
derided
it
as
sounding
underproduced,
dull
and
lacklustre.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
March
2001
Depeche
Mode
held
a
press
conference
at
the
Valentino
Hotel
in
<a
href="/wiki/Hamburg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>
to
announce
the
<a
href="/wiki/Exciter_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Exciter
Tour">Exciter
Tour</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
total
the
tour
featured
84
performances
for
over
1.5
million
fans
in
24
countries.<sup
id="cite_ref-70"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
concerts
held
in
Paris
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Palais_Omnisports_de_Paris-Bercy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Palais
Omnisports
de
Paris-Bercy">Palais
Omnisports
de
Paris-Bercy</a>
were
filmed
and
later
released
in
May
2002
as
a
<a
href="/wiki/Live_CD?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
CD">live
DVD</a>
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Night_in_Paris?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Night
in
Paris">One
Night
in
Paris</a></i>.</p>








<p>In
October
2002
the
band
won
the
first-ever
<i>Q</i>
magazine
&quot;Innovation
Award&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2003
Dave
Gahan
released
his
first
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Paper_Monsters?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paper
Monsters">Paper
Monsters</a></i>,
and
toured
to
promote
the
record.
Also
released
in
2003
was
Martin
Gore's
second
solo
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Counterfeit%C2%B2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Counterfeit&sup2;">Counterfeit&sup2;</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
Andrew
Fletcher
also
founded
his
own
record
label,
<a
href="/wiki/Toast_Hawaii_(record_label)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Toast
Hawaii
(record
label)">Toast
Hawaii</a>,
specialising
in
promoting
electronic
music.</p>








<p>A
new
remix
compilation
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Remixes_81%E2%80%9304?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Remixes
81–04">Remixes
81–04</a></i>
was
released
in
2004,
featuring
new
and
unreleased
promo
mixes
of
the
band's
singles
from
1981
to
2004.
A
new
version
of
&quot;Enjoy
the
Silence&quot;,
remixed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Shinoda?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Shinoda">Mike
Shinoda</a>,
entitled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Enjoy_the_Silence_04?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Enjoy
the
Silence
04"
class="mw-redirect">Enjoy
the
Silence
04</a>&quot;
was
released
as
a
single
and
reached
No.
7
on
the
UK
charts.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Playing_the_Angel_.282005.E2.80.932007.29"><i>Playing
the
Angel</i>
(2005–2007)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12"
title="Edit
section:
Playing
the
Angel
(2005–2007)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="/wiki?title=Special:Upload&amp;wpDestFile=Bremen_2006_Depeche_Mode_by-RaBoe.jpg"
class="new"
title="File:Bremen
2006
Depeche
Mode
by-RaBoe.jpg">File:Bremen
2006
Depeche
Mode
by-RaBoe.jpg</a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">










<a
href="/wiki/Touring_the_Angel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touring
the
Angel">Touring
the
Angel</a>
concert
in











<a
href="/wiki/Bremen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bremen">Bremen</a>,
June
2006









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>In
October
2005,
the
band
released
their
11th
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Playing_the_Angel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Playing
the
Angel">Playing
the
Angel</a></i>.
Produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Ben_Hillier?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ben
Hillier">Ben
Hillier</a>
the
album
peaked
at
No.
1
in
18
countries
and
featured
the
hit
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Precious_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Precious
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Precious</a>&quot;.
This
is
the
first
Depeche
Mode
album
to
feature
lyrics
written
by
Gahan
and,
consequently,
the
first
album
since
1984's
<i><a
href="/wiki/Some_Great_Reward?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Some
Great
Reward">Some
Great
Reward</a></i>
featuring
songs
not
written
by
Gore.
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Suffer_Well?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suffer
Well">Suffer
Well</a>&quot;,
was
the
first
ever
post-Clarke
Depeche
Mode
single
not
to
be
written
by
Gore
(lyrics
by
Gahan,
music
by
Philpott/Eigner).
The
final
single
from
the
album
was
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/John_the_Revelator_/_Lilian?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
the
Revelator
/
Lilian">John
the
Revelator</a>&quot;,
an
uptempo
electronic
track
with
a
running
religious
theme,
accompanied
by
&quot;Lilian&quot;,
a
lush
track
that
was
a
hit
in
many
clubs
all
over
the
world.</p>








<p>To
promote
<i>Playing
the
Angel</i>
the
band
launched
<a
href="/wiki/Touring_the_Angel?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touring
the
Angel">Touring
the
Angel</a>,
a
concert
tour
of
Europe
and
North
America
that
began
in
November
2005
and
ran
for
nine
months.
During
the
last
two
legs
of
the
tour
Depeche
Mode
headlined
a
number
of
festivals
including
the
<a
href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival">Coachella
Valley
Music
and
Arts
Festival</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Wireless_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wireless
Festival">O<sub>2</sub>
Wireless
Festival</a>.
In
total
the
band
played
to
more
than
2.8
million
people
across
31
countries
and
the
tour
was
one
of
the
highest
grossing
and
critically
acclaimed
tours
of
2005/06.<sup
id="cite_ref-billboard1_2-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard1-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
Speaking
about
the
tour,
Gahan
praised
it
as
<i>&quot;probably
the
most
enjoyable,
rewarding
live
shows
we've
ever
done.
The
new
material
was
just
waiting
to
be
played
live.
It
took
on
a
life
of
its
own.
With
the
energy
of
the
crowds,
it
just
came
to
life&quot;</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
shows
at
<a
href="/wiki/Milan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Milan">Milan's</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Mediolanum_Forum?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mediolanum
Forum">Fila
Forum</a>
were
filmed
and
edited
into
a
concert
film
which
was
released
on
DVD
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Touring_the_Angel:_Live_in_Milan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Touring
the
Angel:
Live
in
Milan">Touring
the
Angel:
Live
in
Milan</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>A
&quot;best-of&quot;
compilation
was
released
in
November
2006,
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Best_Of,_Volume_1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Best
Of,
Volume
1"
class="mw-redirect">The
Best
Of,
Volume
1</a></i>
featuring
a
new
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Martyr_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Martyr
(song)">Martyr</a>&quot;,
an
outtake
from
the
<i>Playing
the
Angel</i>
sessions.
Later
that
month
Depeche
Mode
received
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards_2006?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Europe
Music
Awards
2006"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Europe
Music
Award</a>
in
the
Best
Group
category.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2006,
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Complete_Depeche_Mode?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Complete
Depeche
Mode"
class="mw-redirect">The
Complete
Depeche
Mode</a></i>
as
its
fourth
ever
digital
box-set
(following
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Complete_U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Complete
U2">The
Complete
U2</a></i>
in
2004,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Complete_Stevie_Wonder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Complete
Stevie
Wonder">The
Complete
Stevie
Wonder</a></i>
in
2005,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan:_The_Collection?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Dylan:
The
Collection">Bob
Dylan:
The
Collection</a></i>
earlier
in
2006).<sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
August
2007,
during
promotion
for
Dave
Gahan's
second
solo
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Hourglass_(Dave_Gahan_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hourglass
(Dave
Gahan
album)">Hourglass</a></i>,
it
was
announced
that
Depeche
Mode
were
heading
back
in
studio
in
early
2008
to
work
on
a
new
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Sounds_of_the_Universe_.282008.E2.80.932011.29"><i>Sounds
of
the
Universe</i>
(2008–2011)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13"
title="Edit
section:
Sounds
of
the
Universe
(2008–2011)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
May
2008,
the
band
returned
to
the
studio
with
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Ben_Hillier?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ben
Hillier">Ben
Hillier</a>
to
work
on
some
songs
that
Martin
Gore
had
demoed
at
his
home
studio
in
<a
href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Santa
Barbara,
California">Santa
Barbara,
California</a>.
Later
that
year
it
was
announced
that
Depeche
Mode
were
splitting
from
their
long-term
US
label,
Warner
Music,
and
signing
with
<a
href="/wiki/EMI_Music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="EMI
Music"
class="mw-redirect">EMI
Music</a>
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>On
15
January
2009,
the
official
Depeche
Mode
website
announced
that
the
band's
12th
studio
album
would
be
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sounds_of_the_Universe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sounds
of
the
Universe">Sounds
of
the
Universe</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
was
released
in
April
2009,
it
was
also
made
available
through
an
iTunes
Pass,
where
the
buyer
received
individual
tracks
in
the
weeks
leading
up
to
official
release
date.
Andy
Fletcher
says
the
idea
for
their
iTunes
Pass
was
a
combination
of
the
band's
and
iTunes':
&quot;I
think
the
digital
and
record
companies
are
starting
to
get
their
act
together.
They
were
very
lazy
in
the
first
10
years
when
downloads
came
in.
Now
they're
collaborating
more
and
coming
up
with
interesting
ideas
for
fans
to
buy
products.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
went
to
number
one
in
21
countries.
Critical
response
was
generally
positive
and
it
was
nominated
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy</a>
in
the
&quot;Best
Alternative
Album&quot;
category.<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wrong_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wrong
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Wrong</a>&quot;
was
the
first
single
from
the
album,
released
digitally
in
February
2009.
Subsequent
singles
were
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Peace_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Peace
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Peace</a>&quot;
and
the
double
a-side
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Fragile_Tension_/_Hole_to_Feed?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Fragile
Tension
/
Hole
to
Feed">Fragile
Tension
/
Hole
to
Feed</a>&quot;.
In
addition,
&quot;Perfect&quot;
was
released
as
a
promotional-only
(non-commercial)
single
in
the
US.</p>








<p>Depeche
Mode
performed
on
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jimmy
Kimmel
Live!">Jimmy
Kimmel
Live!</a>&quot;
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Boulevard?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hollywood
Boulevard">Hollywood
Boulevard</a>
in
Los
Angeles
on
23
April
2009,
drawing
more
than
12,000
fans,
which
was
the
largest
audience
the
show
had
ever
seen
since
premiering
in
2003.<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
May
2009
the
band
embarked
on
a
concert
tour
in
support
of
the
album
–
called
<a
href="/wiki/Tour_of_the_Universe_(tour)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tour
of
the
Universe
(tour)">Tour
of
the
Universe</a>,
it
had
been
announced
at
a
press
conference
in
October
2008
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Olympiastadion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Olympiastadion"
class="mw-redirect">Olympiastadion</a>
in
Berlin.<sup
id="cite_ref-83"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>
There
was
a
warm
up
show
in
<a
href="/wiki/Luxembourg?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>
and
it
officially
started
on
10
May
2009
in
<a
href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tel
Aviv">Tel
Aviv</a>.
The
first
leg
of
the
tour
was
disrupted
when
Dave
Gahan
was
struck
down
with
<a
href="/wiki/Gastroenteritis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Gastroenteritis">gastroenteritis</a>.
During
treatment
doctors
found
and
removed
a
low
grade
tumour
from
the
singer's
bladder.
Gahan's
illness
caused
16
concerts
to
be
cancelled,
but
several
of
the
shows
were
rescheduled
for
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-84"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
headlined
the
<a
href="/wiki/Lollapalooza?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a>
festival
during
the
North
American
leg
of
the
tour.
The
tour
also
took
the
band
back
to
South
America
for
the
first
time
since
1994's
<a
href="/wiki/Exotic_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Exotic
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">Exotic
Tour</a>.
During
the
final
European
leg
the
band
played
a
show
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Royal
Albert
Hall">Royal
Albert
Hall</a>
in
aid
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Teenage_Cancer_Trust?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Teenage
Cancer
Trust">Teenage
Cancer
Trust</a>,
where
former
member
Alan
Wilder
joined
Martin
Gore
on
stage
for
a
performance
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Somebody_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Somebody
(Depeche
Mode
song)"
class="mw-redirect">Somebody</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-85"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-86"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
total
the
band
played
to
more
than
2.7
million
people
across
32
countries
and
the
tour
was
one
of
the
most
profitable
in
America
in
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-87"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
concerts
held
at
<a
href="/wiki/Palau_Sant_Jordi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Palau
Sant
Jordi">Palau
Sant
Jordi</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Barcelona,_Spain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Barcelona,
Spain"
class="mw-redirect">Barcelona,
Spain</a>
were
filmed
and
later
released
on
DVD
and
<a
href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blu-ray
Disc">Blu-ray
Disc</a>
release
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Tour_of_the_Universe_:_Barcelona_20/21.11.09?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tour
of
the
Universe
:
Barcelona
20/21.11.09"
class="mw-redirect">Tour
of
the
Universe
:
Barcelona
20/21.11.09</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
March
2010,
Depeche
Mode
won
the
award
for
&quot;Best
International
Group
–
Rock
/
Pop&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Echo_(music_award)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Echo
(music
award)">ECHO
Awards</a>
in
Germany.<sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>As
a
conclusion
of
the
3-year
working
relationship
with
<a
href="/wiki/EMI?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"

<i><a

<p>Depeche

<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Delta_Machine_.282012.E2.80.93present.29"><i>Delta
Machine</i>
(2012–present)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14"
title="Edit
section:
Delta
Machine
(2012–present)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
October
2012
during
a
press
conference
in
<a
href="/wiki/Paris?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Paris">Paris</a>,
Dave
Gahan,
Martin
Gore
and
Andy
Fletcher
announced
plans
to
release
a
new
album
and
a
worldwide
<a
href="/wiki/The_Delta_Machine_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Delta
Machine
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">tour</a>
starting
from
<a
href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tel
Aviv">Tel
Aviv</a>
and
continuing
in
Europe
and
North
America
in
the
year
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-98"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup>
Martin
Gore
revealed
that
Flood
mixed
the
album,
marking
the
producer's
first
studio
collaboration
with
the
band
since
1993's
<i>Songs
of
Faith
and
Devotion</i>.</p>








<p>In
December
2012,
the
band
officially
announced
signing
a
worldwide
deal
with
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>
and
releasing
a
new
album
in
March
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-99"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
24
January
2013,
it
was
confirmed
that
the
album
was
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Delta_Machine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Delta
Machine">Delta
Machine</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-100"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Heaven_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Heaven
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Heaven</a>&quot;,
the
debut
single
from
<i>Delta
Machine</i>
was
released
commercially
on
Friday
1
February
2013
(although
not
in
the
UK).
The
release
date
in
the
UK
was
pushed
back
to
18
March
2013
(17
March
2013
on
iTunes),
currently
with
no
explanation.
Bafflingly,
the
physical
release
still
bore
the
Mute
Records
logo,
even
though
the
band
have
now
severed
ties
with
their
long
standing
label.
Andy
Fletcher
mentioned
in
an
interview
this
was
due
to
their
&quot;devotion&quot;
to
the
label
and
with
the
band's
insistence.</p>








<p>In
March,
the
band
announced
North
American
dates
to
its
<a
href="/wiki/The_Delta_Machine_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Delta
Machine
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">'Delta
Machine'
summer
tour</a>,
starting
22
August
from
<a
href="/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Detroit,
Michigan"
class="mw-redirect">Detroit</a>
and
ending
8
October
in
<a
href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phoenix,
Arizona">Phoenix</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-101"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
June,
other
European
dates<sup
id="cite_ref-102"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup>
were
confirmed
for
early
2014.</p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Artistry">Artistry</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15"
title="Edit
section:
Artistry">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style">Musical
style</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Depeche
Mode
drew
its
artistic
influences
from
a
wide
range
of
artists,
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Kraftwerk?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kraftwerk">Kraftwerk</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-103"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/David_Bowie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Bowie">David
Bowie</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Clash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Clash">The
Clash</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-104"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blues">blues
music</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-105"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grunge?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grunge">American
grunge
scene</a><sup
id="cite_ref-contactm1_57-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-contactm1-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Velvet_Underground?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Velvet
Underground"
class="mw-redirect">Velvet
Underground</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-106"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
genres
Depeche
Mode
are
typically
associated
with
include
<a
href="/wiki/Synthpop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Synthpop">synthpop</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_dance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
dance">alternative
dance</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/New_wave_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
wave
music">new
wave</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>.</p>








<p>Depeche
Mode
were
recognised
in
their
early
years
as
a
synthpop
band
and
were
considered
teen
idols.
Following
the
departure
of
<a
href="/wiki/Vince_Clarke?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vince
Clarke">Vince
Clarke</a>,
their
music
began
to
take
on
a
darker
tone
as
Martin
Gore
assumed
lead
songwriting
duties.
Gore's
lyrical
artistry
has
been
recognised
as
encapsulating
themes
such
as
sex,
religion,
politics,
racism
and
socialism,<sup
id="cite_ref-107"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup>
so
much
so
that
many
labeled
the
band's
lyrical
and
musical
themes
as
dark
and
bleak.
In
response,
Gore
stated
he
feels
lyrical
themes
which
tackle
issues
related
to
solitude
and
loneliness
present
more
of
a
realistic
character
and
are
a
better
representation
of
reality,
whereas
he
finds
'happy
songs'
fake
and
unrealistic.<sup
id="cite_ref-108"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup>
Gore
also
added;
&quot;I've
never
seen
our
music
as
being
over-dark.
I
think
that
there
is
always
an
element
of
hope
in
our
music.&quot;
<sup
id="cite_ref-109"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="mw-headline"

class="mw-editsection">[<a

title="Edit
section:
Influence">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Depeche
Mode
have
been
recognised
as
making
a
significant
impact
on
the
development
of
various
popular
music
genres,

to
many

citing
them
as
an
inspiration

(but

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Legacy">Legacy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Depeche_Mode&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18"
title="Edit
section:
Legacy">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
boilerplate
seealso">








See
also:









<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Depeche_Mode_covers?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
Depeche
Mode
covers"
class="mw-redirect">List
of
Depeche
Mode
covers</a>







</div>








<p>One
of
the
most
influential
musical
groups
over
the
past
three
decades,
Depeche
Mode
have
released
a
total
of
thirteen
studio
albums,
ten
compilation
albums,
six
live
albums,
eight
box
sets,
thirteen
video
albums,
seventy
music
videos
and
fifty-three
singles.
The
band
have
sold
over
100
million
records
and
have
played
to
in
excess
of
30
million
people,
making
them
one
of
the
world's
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">best
selling
music
artists</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-billboard1_2-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard1-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Q_.28magazine.29_3-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Q_.28magazine.29-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
have
had
forty-eight
songs
in
the
UK
Singles
Chart,
one
US
and
two
UK
number
one
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-127"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
album
<a
href="/wiki/Songs_of_Faith_and_Devotion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songs
of
Faith
and
Devotion">Songs
of
Faith
and
Devotion</a>
hit
#1
in
the
UK
and
USA
simultaneously,
making
them
one
of
only
eleven
UK
acts
to
do
so,
the
others
being
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Rod_Stewart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rod
Stewart">Rod
Stewart</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pink
Floyd">Pink
Floyd</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Lennon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Lennon">John
Lennon</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Phil_Collins?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Phil
Collins">Phil
Collins</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Radiohead?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Radiohead">Radiohead</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Coldplay?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Susan_Boyle?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Susan
Boyle">Susan
Boyle</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Adele?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adele">Adele</a>.
In
addition,
all
of
their
studio
albums
have
reached
the
UK
Top
10
and
their
albums
have
spent
over
210
weeks
on
the
UK
Charts.<sup
id="cite_ref-128"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Music
critic
<a
href="/wiki/Sasha_Frere-Jones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sasha
Frere-Jones">Sasha
Frere-Jones</a>
claimed
that
&quot;the
last
serious
English
influence
was
Depeche
Mode,
who
seem
more
and
more
significant
as
time
passes.&quot;
<sup
id="cite_ref-129"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup>
Depeche
Mode
have
been
nominated
for
five
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>;
<a
href="/wiki/Devotional_(video)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Devotional
(video)">Devotional</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Long_Form_Music_Video?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Long
Form
Music
Video"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Long
Form
Music
Video</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/I_Feel_Loved?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Feel
Loved">I
Feel
Loved</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Suffer_Well?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Suffer
Well">Suffer
Well</a>,
both
for
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Dance_Recording?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Dance
Recording"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Dance
Recording</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sounds_of_the_Universe?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sounds
of
the
Universe">Sounds
of
the
Universe</a>
for
Best
Alternative
Album
and
<a
href="/wiki/Wrong_(Depeche_Mode_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wrong
(Depeche
Mode
song)">Wrong</a>
for
Best
Short
Form
Music
Video.
In
addition,
Depeche
Mode
have
been
honoured
with
a
<a
href="/wiki/Brit_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brit
Award"
class="mw-redirect">Brit
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Enjoy_The_Silence?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Enjoy
The
Silence"
class="mw-redirect">Enjoy
The
Silence</a>
in
the
Best
British
Single
category,
the
first
ever
Q
Magazine
Innovation
Award
and
an
Ivor
Novello
Award
for
<a
href="/wiki/Martin_Gore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Martin
Gore">Martin
Gore</a>
in
the
category
of
International
Achievement.</p>








<p>Depeche
Mode
are
frequently
praised
by
the
music
press;
they
became
&quot;The
most
popular
electronic
band
the
world
has
ever
known&quot;
according
to
<i>Q</i>
magazine,
&quot;One
of
the
greatest
British
pop
groups
of
all
time&quot;
according
to
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sunday_Telegraph?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sunday
Telegraph"
class="mw-redirect">Sunday
Telegraph</a></i>,<sup
id="cite_ref-130"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-131"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
&quot;The
quintessential
eighties
techno-pop
band&quot;
according
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
magazine<sup
id="cite_ref-132"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
<i>MTV</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-133"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup>
Depeche
Mode
were
ranked
#2
on
Electronic
Music
Realm's
list
of
The
100
Greatest
Artists
of
Electronic
Music,<sup
id="cite_ref-134"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup>
#3
in
a
list
of
The
Most
Influential
Electronic
Music
Pioneers
by
Ranker,<sup
id="cite_ref-135"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup>
the
band
were
also
ranked
#144
on
Acclaimed
Music's
list
of
Top
1000
Artists
of
All
Time
<sup
id="cite_ref-136"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
Q
Magazine
included
them
on
their
list
of
50
artists
who
changed
the
world.<sup
id="cite_ref-137"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

render_ads(false,
window['ad_config_bot']);





function
afc_match()
{








var
count
=
-1;








if(window['ad_config_top'])
{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Depeche_Mode&page=1&ac=24&qid=EDAA63B08C3FD7662DBBEFD815944C29&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();

fashion

fashion.
